  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1b2d69ff-1c0a-41fb-9f38-3f3c8075fea8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

Signed with the initials NRR, the telegram launches a race to uncover a treasure stolen by the Nazis and the truth behind the murder of the last Russian royal family. All too soon, the treasure hunt starts to smell like a Lucian trap. But the bait might just be irresistible...what will Amy and Dan risk to find out what <i>really</i> happened on the night their parents died?</span>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/611783-do-you-need-to-read-the-series-in-order-or">Do you need to read the series in order or can you just pick up one in the middle?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_611783'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F6255144-the-black-circle">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/611783-do-you-need-to-read-the-series-in-order-or">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/611783-do-you-need-to-read-the-series-in-order-or">Add your answer</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/2918779-asterop"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1601168663i/2918779._UY100_CR5,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/2918779-asterop">Asteropê</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I'd say you do need to read them in order! Each book ends on a cliffhanger, basically and the clues in each book leads to the clues in the next one. T<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I'd say you do need to read them in order! Each book ends on a cliffhanger, basically and the clues in each book leads to the clues in the next one. Things that occurred in one book are referenced in the next. The series is more like one long story, broken into 10 books and written by different authors. I just finished reading 1-3 back to back and they all flow into each other. It would be confusing and a bit weird to read #10, then #2, and then #5. And it'd equally be confusing and weird to just read #5 and no other book. It'd be like watching the middle 20 minutes of a movie and not the beginning or end or the two middle episodes of the TV show 24, without watching any of the others. You'd miss the plot, content and greater meaning of things. I think with this series, it's necessary to read them in order to enjoy and understand things fully. ;-) <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerFooter'>

</div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer274700630" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15703711488811561032">The best installment so far! The story is very exciting with much interesting information about the Romanovs. Amy and Dan finally managed to persuade one of their opponents to cooperate, and they also gained a powerful ally. Ian and Natalie failed badly, and Irina is weirder than ever. <br/>I want the next book! <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1408044174i/10801259.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>On the far end there stood a massive statue of a woman holding a sword over her head, rising like a skyscraper into the cloudy horizon. They'd seen it in the distance as they raced across </i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText15703711488811561032" style="display:none">The best installment so far! The story is very exciting with much interesting information about the Romanovs. Amy and Dan finally managed to persuade one of their opponents to cooperate, and they also gained a powerful ally. Ian and Natalie failed badly, and Irina is weirder than ever. <br>I want the next book! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1408044174i/10801259.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>On the far end there stood a massive statue of a woman holding a sword over her head, rising like a skyscraper into the cloudy horizon. They'd seen it in the distance as they raced across the city, but up close it was a frightening spectacle."The Motherland Calls," said Amy. "It's twice as tall as the Statue of Liberty. Do you know what it commemorates?"<br>"Don't have a clue, but I'm sure you're going to tell me."</i>
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_99665233" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99665233" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1735763-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442495481p2/1735763.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/99665233?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/1735763-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99665233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3297807195615661992">I am now halfway through this exciting series, which ends with Book Ten coming out August 2010. The Black Circle begins with a telegram that lures to Russia 11 year-old Dan Cahill and 14 year-old Amy Cahill—a brother and sister team who are in the race to uncover the 39 clues leading to great power. I must admit I had flashbacks of James Bond spy movies as I read this book.<br/><br/>What caught my interest this time is that Dan and Amy go through a whole risky adventure, even traveling from Cairo to Russi</span>
  <span id="freeText3297807195615661992" style="display:none">I am now halfway through this exciting series, which ends with Book Ten coming out August 2010. The Black Circle begins with a telegram that lures to Russia 11 year-old Dan Cahill and 14 year-old Amy Cahill—a brother and sister team who are in the race to uncover the 39 clues leading to great power. I must admit I had flashbacks of James Bond spy movies as I read this book.<br /><br />What caught my interest this time is that Dan and Amy go through a whole risky adventure, even traveling from Cairo to Russia on their own without Nellie, their au pair. Instead, it is the Holts, particularly Hamilton, who assists them, working together with them to uncover the next clue. A camaraderie even forms between them by the end.<br /><br />My maternal instincts, of course, rebelled against the fact that they were unchaperoned by an adult throughout their dangerous mission, but my reader and writer instincts tell me this was done for a reason. It emphasized the reality of their orphaned state and how they were unknowingly prepped by their grandmother Grace to take on this challenge. And adults who have been aware of the 39 clues for years assisted them in other ways. Throughout the whole book I wondered why Nellie was not involved, and then something occurs toward the end that leaves the reader wondering about her role in all of this.<br /><br />The Lucian stronghold is the one we learn about this time and like all the other strongholds, there is always its powerful leader ready to strike their rivals. The force of the Madrigals, their enemy, is felt strongly too as Dan and Amy race with them close on their heels, along with the rest of the extended family who is taking part in the hunt. The man in black that makes a brief but sinister appearance in all the books does so again at a crucial moment (as usual), raising yet again the big question as to who he represents exactly. We also wonder more about Irina Spasky whose past loss cause an internal struggle for her and affect her actions.<br /><br />Clearly, the clues that will answer all these questions are undoubtedly scattered throughout the books from the start, making me want to go back and reread them all. But for now I’ll just move on to Book Six.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3297807195615661992" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14832525529563698866">Maybe 3.5 stars......I have mixed feelings about this book in the series. There were two things I really liked about the book. First, I enjoyed the history part taking place in Russia. the details included would easily appeal to kids reading the book, I would imagine. I know the books aren't meant to be plausible, but I think there should be logical explan</span>
  <span id="freeText14832525529563698866" style="display:none">Maybe 3.5 stars......I have mixed feelings about this book in the series. There were two things I really liked about the book. First, I enjoyed the history part taking place in Russia. the details included would easily appeal to kids reading the book, I would imagine. And second, I thought the pace was good - lots of action and a few more details falling into place.<br />But - some items fell flat, in my opinion. I know the books aren't meant to be plausible, but I think there should be logical explanations as to how other team members manage to find out where Amy and Dan are heading. I don't like the fact that they just show up in the same place. Something is missing. Also,I can't remember the kids' exact ages, but I believe Dan is like 11 and Amy 14 - and he manages to drive a motorbike and she drives a car and truck....... stuff like that didn't happen in the earlier books. And, even worse, the disguise Dan is provided with is a mustache and goatee to make him look like an adult??????? I think the author could have come up with something more believable.</span>

<div id="review_85763242" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/85763242" />
    <a title="cherryblossomjen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3084036-cherryblossomjen"><img alt="cherryblossomjen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262109118p2/3084036.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/85763242?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="cherryblossomjen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="cherryblossomjen" href="/user/show/3084036-cherryblossomjen">cherryblossomjen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer85763242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15977340828560621300">As far as I know, <u>The Black Circle</u> marks the halfway point for the 39 clues series. And while this was definitely one of the better books, I find myself able to list more things I *don't* like about the series, than I do. (Note: these comments are more about the books in general, rather than <u>The Black Circle</u> particularly).<br/><br/><i>The writing</i>. On the plus side, having a bunch of different writers take a turn does add various dimensions of flavor, but it's also a bit disconcerting. Sometimes the transitio</span>
  <span id="freeText15977340828560621300" style="display:none">As far as I know, <u>The Black Circle</u> marks the halfway point for the 39 clues series. And while this was definitely one of the better books, I find myself able to list more things I *don't* like about the series, than I do. (Note: these comments are more about the books in general, rather than <u>The Black Circle</u> particularly).<br /><br /><i>The writing</i>. On the plus side, having a bunch of different writers take a turn does add various dimensions of flavor, but it's also a bit disconcerting. Sometimes the transition is seamless, but more often you notice the shift and have to adjust accordingly. <br /><br /><i>The clues.</i> I'll admit--I want to know the mysterious of what the clues add up to. It seems almost like alchemy. But I suspect it has some kind of sentimental moral laced in as part of the treasure too. And I'm fine with that. Honestly, I hope it's something big and not another let down. But I wish the clues were such that you could actually follow along with them logically. For the most part each book is a kind of roller coaster and you have to just sit and wait until the ride stops to see where you end up. I like puzzles you can participate in. But then I don't play the game online, if I did I might feel more like a player instead of a spectator.<br /><br /><i>The characters.</i> Amy bores me. And Dan, while more interesting than his sister, and sometimes very amusing, can also come off as pretty annoying. Their relationship isn't terribly intriguing and maybe it's just me--but I haven't seen either of them grow much over the last few books. On the other hand, the supporting characters--Irina, Oh, Hamilton, and even the Kabras--have internal conflicts that make them complex and interesting. I think those characters are why I keep reading these books, despite my lack of enthusiasm for the protagonists.<br /><br />Honestly, <u>The Black Circle</u> had great pacing, some nice interaction with Irina, Hamilton and featured a new cameo I won't spoil you for. I enjoyed it. There's still room for the series to grow though, and I'm hoping it does.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15977340828560621300" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/879591-sara?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70954514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6512875579282765033">Not the worst book in the 39 clues series so far, but also not the best. In this, Amy and Dan find themselves traveling to Russia (without their au pair) and following clues that a mysterious benefactor has left them, eventually having to work together with another team in the race to solve the puzzle in the time limit they're given. <br/><br/>I <i>loved</i> the fact that this took place in Russia and featured all sorts of Russian history. Anyone unfamiliar with Russian history will be floored at all the things </span>
  <span id="freeText6512875579282765033" style="display:none">Not the worst book in the 39 clues series so far, but also not the best. In this, Amy and Dan find themselves traveling to Russia (without their au pair) and following clues that a mysterious benefactor has left them, eventually having to work together with another team in the race to solve the puzzle in the time limit they're given. <br /><br />I <i>loved</i> the fact that this took place in Russia and featured all sorts of Russian history. Anyone unfamiliar with Russian history will be floored at all the things that took place there. There were also a lot of very cute parts to the book, such as Hamilton Holt nicknaming himself "Hammer" - how can you not laugh at that? But unfortunately, there were also less than stellar parts of the book. I had a hard time believing that Amy and Dan could put on minimal disguises and pass as adults (especially considering that Dan's, like, 11...) and not only that, but they could easily learn to drive motorbikes and cars. I also didn't like the way their au pair was written out of this book; it felt too fantastical. And the resolution to the clues they're following in Russia felt disappointing, blending fiction with history in a mix that, in my opinion, was not that great. On top of those issues, I felt like this book was not particularly strong in its stand-alone plot. I know this book is in the middle of the 10-book series, but the entire book felt very much like filler material instead of getting me pumped for the next book's release.<br /><br />I'm still planning to read the full series, and I did enjoy this book, but it wasn't nearly as good as it could have been. I imagine that a lot of kids will find it entertaining, though, and be able to overlook the problems I found.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6512875579282765033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer347674992408052724">I'm going to give a generic review of the series. Basically because I'm lazy and don't want to write 39 reviews. Okay, 11.<br/><br/>We finally read Book 1. And then because we liked it so well, the entire series. One son (age 12) has read them all, the second son (also age 12) is on Book 2. And son #3 (age 8) will be starting as soon as he finishes his current book.<br/><br/>I thought the premise of this book very interesting. I loved how they integrated history and geography along with problem-solving skills and c</span>
  <span id="freeText347674992408052724" style="display:none">I'm going to give a generic review of the series. Basically because I'm lazy and don't want to write 39 reviews. Okay, 11.<br /><br />We finally read Book 1. And then because we liked it so well, the entire series. One son (age 12) has read them all, the second son (also age 12) is on Book 2. And son #3 (age 8) will be starting as soon as he finishes his current book.<br /><br />I thought the premise of this book very interesting. I loved how they integrated history and geography along with problem-solving skills and code cracking. Add in the action, humor and intrigue and kids (and some adults) can't put them down. All three of us that have read 39 Clues thought Book 2 the weakest of the series. But as one son said, after finishing the series, "Gordon Korman seems to be getting better. I think he's a decent author now." <br /><br />Some of the books are better at teaching the history part, others just barely skim the surface and you don't really learn about the person they're 'highlighting'. I appreciate that they're clean books - no curse words or you-know-what going on. There is some violence (very little, if any, blood) and several murder attempts, but they never work.<br /><br />The series would most likely be called twaddle by my Charlotte Mason friends. I do, however, think it has more redeeming qualities than most kids literature and I'm happy to see my boys devouring a book every day or so.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2816006501760555464">I have enjoyed each and everyone of the books in this series. After the first one this one was probably my favorite. In the past Dan and Amy have been chased by other families but have not formed any alliances that lasted throughout the book. They were double crossed in each one. It was refreshing to see them make an alliance with the Holts that lasted all the way through the book. Irin played a bigger role in this book.   <span id="freeText2816006501760555464" style="display:none">I have enjoyed each and everyone of the books in this series. After the first one this one was probably my favorite. In the past Dan and Amy have been chased by other families but have not formed any alliances that lasted throughout the book. They were double crossed in each one. It was refreshing to see them make an alliance with the Holts that lasted all the way through the book. Irin played a bigger role in this book. She is probably the one character that I have loved to hate. That is changing somewhat. I have seen another side of her and found out a bit more of her past. I actually saw a part of her heart that makes me feel somewhat sorry for her. I was also glad that they had left the babysitter or au pair out of this one. It gave us a chance to see what Dan and Amy could do on their own without her. They actually had to work together more and fight less. I loved the amount of Russian history we learned. I also like the fact that we were not running from one country to another trying to follow the action. The setting was well described and the characters were developed a little more in this book. All I could say to Patrick Carman about this book is “Well done!”</span>

Then I have another question about Amy: how was putting on a wig going to make her look any older than fourteen? Those disguises shouldn't have been able to fool anyone! <span id="freeTextContainer4523357088629074675"><br/><br/>I thought this book 39 Clues” The Black Circle” was the best out of the series so far because of how in depth it gets with the characters and how they face new challenges. A lot of the characters are starting to team up against Dan and Amy.<br/><br/><br/>Dan and Amy get this telegram from an unknown source but there were no clues who it came from.   <span id="freeText4523357088629074675" style="display:none"><br /><br />I thought this book 39 Clues” The Black Circle” was the best out of the series so far because of how in depth it gets with the characters and how they face new challenges. A lot of the characters are starting to team up against Dan and Amy.<br /><br /><br />Dan and Amy get this telegram from an unknown source but there were no clues who it came from. Dan and Amy were then followed to an airport where a telegram told them to go. In the telegram it had an airport locker combination. This is where the next clue would be. The taxi driver that drove Dan and Amy put a tracking device in their bag so Natalie and Ian could follow them. When Dan found the tracking device he want to break it. But Amy then put a device in the baby stroller that was moving. Dan and Amy found their first clue in an airport store inside a crystal ball with gold glitter and a gold key.<br /><br />In the airport locker Dan and Amy found disguises a Visa gold card, and passports.<br /><br />The book 39 Clues “The Black Circle” takes place in modern day Moscow, St.Petersburg, Volgograd Germany, Omsk, Margadan, and Serbia. In the last book it stopped at Margadan, Serbia. <br /><br /><br />Bron is not always better than brain in some of life challenges. The Holts are stronger than anyone in this competition. But Dan and Amy always stay a step ahead of their competition.. <br /><br /> I would recommend this book for eighth grade and up. This book is great for people who don't like to read a lot because this book doesn't have very many pages. The book goes really in depth with the characters.<br /><br /></span>

There they uncover two disguises and two plane tickets to Russia.<br /><br />Hot on their trail are several family members, and while uncovering the tasks to get the clue, Amy and Dan realize that they're not going to be able to solve all the tasks under the time restriction.<br /><br />So they do the unthinkable - they team up with the Holts. They each cover three locations, where they find and solve each piece of the clue before passing along the information.<br /><br />But someone doesn't want them getting too close and they're doing their best to make sure the kids don't find the secret room. Has Amy and Dan's luck run out, or will they put themselves ahead again in the race for the thirty-nine clues?<br /><br />THE BLACK CIRCLE continues with the worldwide treasure hunt that leaves Amy and Dan in a spotlight of danger. Their puzzle-solving skills leave them as the family team to beat. This series is an amazing adventure to devour.</span>

Once there, they start running and don't quit until the end of the book.   <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/66882164" />

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/66882164?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katrina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katrina" href="/user/show/1372540-katrina">Katrina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of the Series and Reluctant Readers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1372540-katrina?shelf=juvenile">juvenile</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1372540-katrina?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1372540-katrina?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer66882164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10016001033446454836">Another great installment in the <i>39 Clues</i> series though I do have a few complaints. I was sad to see Nellie's total lack of involvement in this book and felt Carman created a poor excuse for her absence (dead cell phone battery-lame!). I was also very disappointed in the inclusion of NRR. I always found it appealing that the kids were able to figure out the clues on their own based on each's particular interests and talents. But in <i>The Black Circle</i> the kids don't figure out a single clue but are</span>
  <span id="freeText10016001033446454836" style="display:none">Another great installment in the <i>39 Clues</i> series though I do have a few complaints. I was sad to see Nellie's total lack of involvement in this book and felt Carman created a poor excuse for her absence (dead cell phone battery-lame!). I was also very disappointed in the inclusion of NRR. I always found it appealing that the kids were able to figure out the clues on their own based on each's particular interests and talents. But in <i>The Black Circle</i> the kids don't figure out a single clue but are given each without them even trying! And the kids, who aren't suppose to trust anyone, never once stop to wonder who NRR is or why he/she is helping them? The book was fast paced and it will certainly keep kids interested in the series but as a whole I didn't think it was as strong as some of the others. Hopefully the next book will be better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10016001033446454836" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14665111955310667307">Pretty good, but everything is way too easy. The pace is fast and furious and mysterious clues are flying all over the place. Some people are helping (or are they?) Dan and Amy, so things are moving more quickly. But they are also figuring out the hints sometimes in mere minutes, a very different case than in the past. It's just a bit discombobulating to have the different authors with different styles, I guess. I enjoyed the bits of Russian history, including a few I'd not known before. I'm sti</span>
  <span id="freeText14665111955310667307" style="display:none">Pretty good, but everything is way too easy. The pace is fast and furious and mysterious clues are flying all over the place. Some people are helping (or are they?) Dan and Amy, so things are moving more quickly. But they are also figuring out the hints sometimes in mere minutes, a very different case than in the past. It's just a bit discombobulating to have the different authors with different styles, I guess. I enjoyed the bits of Russian history, including a few I'd not known before. I'm still a huge fan of the series and recommend it to all tweens and adults who like fun and educational kids books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14665111955310667307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fuHeWRqdGcxPqVDBsS54Nsk5XGurNtgTJkMrzgflZwWlCmlB39c61+eysWlS2K+uW1hdLX5EJzzw4ngPYtCTZQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ib5LXKI6BltjV+3nrXsNP04kSOSU0dhCJepleUUWGUFSVfxEZ3AlQMtMDE9Ojdqn3EVJokGjJ23zSza4ICPtIQ==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer1224538960148131129">I have been a lifelong writer and storyteller. Salem, Oregon is where I spent my formative years and I graduated from Willamette University. After college, I spent a decade living in Portland, Oregon where I worked in advertising, game design, and technology.<br/><br/>I've written young adult and children's books for Scholastic, Little Brown Books For Young Readers and Katherine Tegen Books/ HarperCollins P</span>
  <span id="freeText1224538960148131129" style="display:none">I have been a lifelong writer and storyteller. Salem, Oregon is where I spent my formative years and I graduated from Willamette University. After college, I spent a decade living in Portland, Oregon where I worked in advertising, game design, and technology.<br /><br />I've written young adult and children's books for Scholastic, Little Brown Books For Young Readers and Katherine Tegen Books/ HarperCollins Publishers.<br /><br />I've been fortunate enough to have had some bestselling series work: The Land of Elyon, Atherton, Elliot’s Park, 39 Clues, and Skeleton Creek. Here's a fun note...the books have been translated into approximately two dozen languages. Currently I'm developing a few new-media projects. Check out <a href="http://enterdarkeden.com" rel="nofollow noopener">DARK EDEN</a> to experience this type of cross-platform project.<br /><br />When I'm not writing or creating a story, I spend my free time supporting literacy campaigns and community organizations, fly fishing, playing basketball and tennis, doing crosswords, watching movies, dabbling in video games, reading (lots), and (more than anything else) spending time with my wife and two daughters.</span>
